тАШрдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдпрдордиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛- рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рд░рд╛рджреНрдпреИрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдкрд╛рд░реНрд╡рддреА рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рджреНрд╡реЗ рд╡рд╛рдЪреЗ рд╕рдВрд╕рд░реНрдкрд░реНрдпреИ рдЪрддрд╕реНрд░реЛ рд░рдерд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╕реНрддреБрддрдпреЛрд╜рдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рд╢рд╛рдкрд╛рд╕реНрддрд╛ рд╡рд╕рд┐рд╖реНрдарджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рд┐рдгреНрдпреЛ рди рд╡рд╕рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рджрд╢рдореАрд╖реЛрдбрд╢реНрдпреМ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпреМ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реА рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реА рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реАрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реАрджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реНрдпреЛрд╜рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднреЛрд╜рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджрд╢реА рдмреГрд╣рддреА ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ ред рджрд╢рдореА рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реА рдЪ рджреНрд╡реЗ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпреМ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реА рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реА рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢реАрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реАрджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реНрдпрд╕реНрддрд┐рд╕реНрд░реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрднреЛрд╜рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рджрд╢реА рдмреГрд╣рддреА рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГред рдЖрджреНрдпреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдкрд░реНрд╡рддрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрд╛ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢реАрд╖реЛрдбрд╢реНрдпреМ рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрджреЗрд╡рддреНрдпреЗ рддрджреБрддреНрддрд░рд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддрд╕реНрд░реЛ рд░рдерд╛рдЩреНрдЧрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрд╛рдГ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдРрдиреНрджреНрд░реНрдпрдГ рее

+Jamison Brereton

53 (287)
Indra, etc.
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
24 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 10, 16; anuс╣гс╣нubh 12, 20, 22; g─Бyatr─л 13; br╠еhat─л 18
This sprawling hymn, a supplement to the Indra collection, consists of at least six different sections in five different meters. There is little or no connection among the parts, which were probably originally independent. However, the whole seems intended to glorify the poet Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra and his family, the Ku┼Ыikas, as well as his patron, King Sud─Бs, and the Bharatas. Moreover, several of the different parts have clear reminiscences of other hymns in the Indra cycle of this maс╣Зс╕Нala, and so the hymn serves as a sort of summary of the themes of this Indra collection.
The beginning of the hymn (vss. 1тАУ6) is the most conventional part, with its invitation to Indra to come to our ritual with gifts and to drink the soma. The most interesting feature is the mention of the pleasures of wife and home (vss. 4тАУ6) and the envoi to Indra in verse 6, urging him to go home after consuming the soma at our sacrifice. (See also I.82.5тАУ6.) This dismissal seems appropriate to the final hymn of the Indra collection and may in part account for this little hymn being appended here. The next section (vss. 7тАУ14) is subtly soldered to the first: the final word of verse 6 is d├бkс╣гiс╣З─Бvat тАЬaccompanied by priestly gifts,тАЭ while the first phrase of verse 7 is im├й bhoj─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬthese benefactorsтАЭтАФthe word bhoj├б is used through out the hymn devoted to the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б (X.106) to refer to the bestowers of the priestly gifts. The whole of this second section concerns the relationship of the poet Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra and his family with his patron, King Sud─Бs and his people, the Bharatas, via the mediation of Indra, whose powers the poet can command for the sake of Sud─Бs and his subjects because of his poetic gifts. There are several reminiscences of previous Indra hymns in III. Verse 7, with the patrons com
pared to the Aс╣Еgirases, recalls the extensive treatment of the Aс╣Еgirases in III.31. Verse 9 gives a synopsis of III.33, in which Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra stops the rivers flowing so Sud─Бs and his troops can cross; the name Sud─Бs is mentioned in this story only here. Vi┼Ыv─БmitraтАЩs family, the Ku┼Ыikas, are found here in verses 9тАУ11; in III.33.5 he calls himself тАЬthe son of Ku┼Ыika,тАЭ and a repeated verse containing the plural of the name serves as a ring-compositional marker for the whole of the Indra cycle of Maс╣Зс╕Нala III (III.30.20 = III.50.4), as discussed in the introduction to the latter hymn. This section ends with a slighting mention of a rival and appar ently non-sacrificing group, whom Indra is urged to subjugate to Sud─Бs and the Bharatas.
The next two verses (15тАУ16) are the most mysterious in the hymn; they both concern a female figure identified as sasarpar─л╠Б, the formation and etymology of which is unclear and which may either be a proper name or an attributive charac terizing adjective. (Our translation, тАЬthe squirming, sappy (cow called) Sasarpar─л,тАЭ is a portmanteau containing both adjectives evoked by the phonology and mor phology of the word and the proper name; we consider it a multiple semi-pun.) The Anukramaс╣З─л assigns these two verses to V─Бc [=тАЬspeechтАЭ] Sasarpar─л, and some scholars consider that the figure the embodiment of the Ku┼ЫikasтАЩ verbal art. In any case she seems to be responsible for the fame of the people she aids.
The next four verses (17тАУ20) appear to have no connection with the rest of the hymn. They are prayers to deflect various possible catastrophes that might befall a team of oxen and the vehicle they pull on a journey, and wish for safe return. This section reads as if it were a continuation of or expansion on the Zauberspruch at the end of III.33 against potential difficulties afflicting a team and its wagon at a ford.
The final four verses (21тАУ24) are very difficult to interpret. They have tradition ally been taken as the expression of the implacable hostility between Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra and Vasiс╣гс╣нha, which is a staple of later texts (e.g., the Mah─Бbh─Бrata). But there is no whiff of this personal hostility in the R╠еgveda, in our opinion, and there is certainly no mention of Vasiс╣гс╣нha, direct or indirect, in the verses here. There is, however, hostility: verse 21 calls on Indra to help us defeat our enemy, and the next few verses express in colorful images the impotence of the enemyтАЩs actions and weapons. The most puzzling verse is the final one, where the Bharatas, the people

of Sud─Бs, celebrated in verse 12, appear to be presented in an unflattering light. We have no explanation for this.

English translation:

тАЬIndra and Parvata, bring hither, in a spacious car, delightful viands (genitive rative of) good progeny; partake, deities, of the oblations (offered)at (our) sacrifices, and gratified by the (sacrificial) food, be elevated by our praises.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Indra and тАЬMountainтАЭ [=IndraтАЩs mace?], with a lofty chariot convey hither precious nourishments, providing good heroes.
Pursue the oblations at our ceremonies, o gods. Become strengthened by our hymns, becoming exhilarated on the refreshing drink.

+Griffith

ON a high car, O Parvata and Indra, bring pleasant viands, with brave heroes, hither.
Enjoy the gifts, Gods, at our sacrifices wax strong by hymns, rejoice in our oblation.

English translation:

тАЬTarry a while contentedly, Maghavan (at our rite); go not away; for I offer to you (the libation) of the copiously-effused Soma; powerful Indra, I lay hold of the skirts (of your robe) with sweet-flavoured commendations, as a son (clings to the garment) of a father.тАЭ

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAdhvaryu, let us two offer praise; do you concur with me; let us address plural asing praise to Indra; sit down, Indra, on the sacred grass (prepared by) the instrumental tutor of the rite; and may our commendations be most acceptable to Indra.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Do you concur with me: prati me gс╣Ыс╣З─лhi; the Hot─Б is supposed to speak to Adhvaryu to direct their joint performance of some part of the ceremony

+Jamison Brereton

Let us both recite, Adhvaryu: sing in response to me. Let us both make a vehicle enjoyable to Indra.
Sit right here on the ritual grass of the sacrificer. And then the hymn will be recited to Indra.

+Griffith

Adhvaryu, sing we both; sing thou in answer: make we a laud acceptable to Indra.
Upon this sacrificer’s grass he seated: to Indra shall our eulogy be uttered.

+Geldner

La├Я uns aufsagen, Adhvaryu! Antworte du mir! Wir wollen dem Indra das beliebte Gef├дhrt machen. Setz dich auf das Barhis des opfernden und dann werde dem Indra das Lobgedicht vorgetragen.

+Grassmann

Lasst beid’ uns singen, Priester, sing mir Antwort, dem Indra lasst uns liebes Lob bereiten; Hier setz dich nieder auf die Streu des Opfrers; dann sei dem Indra unser Spruch gesprochen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬA man’s wife, Maghavan, is hiw dwelling; verily she is his plural ce of birth; thither let your horses, harnessed (to your car), convey you; we prepare the Soma at the fit season; may Agni come as our messenger befor eyou.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

His plural ce of birth: j─Бy─Б id astam sedu yoniс╕е: astam = gс╣Ыham (gс╣Ыhiс╣З─л gс╣Ыham ucyate iti smс╣Ыteс╕е; na gс╣Ыham gс╣Ыhamisy─Бhurgс╣Ыhi.с╣Зo gс╣Ыhamucyate)

+Jamison Brereton

Just the wife is the home; she is the womb. Let your yoked fallow bays convey you to it.
Whenever we will press soma, Agni the messenger will run to you.

+Griffith

A wife, O Maghavan is home and dwelling: so let thy Bay Steeds yoked convey thee hither.
Whenever we press out for thee the Soma, let Agni as our Herald speed to call thee.

+Geldner

Die Frau ist das Heim, o Gabenreicher, sie ist der Scho├Я; dahin sollen dich die angeschirrten Falben fahren. So oft wir Soma pressen werden, soll Agni als Bote zu dir eilen.

+Grassmann

Die Frau ist Heimat, sie der Schooss, o Indra; drum m├╢gen dich geschirrt die F├╝chse fahren; Zu welcher Zeit wir beid’ auch Soma pressen, so l├дuft als Bote immer zu dir Agni.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬDepart, Maghavan; come Indra; both ways, protector, there is a motive for you whether it be standing in your vast chariot, or liberating your neighing steed.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Both ways: ubhayatra te artham: Indra’s wife awaits his return, the Soma libation invites his stay; protectorL bhr─Бt─Б = liс╣н, brother; but here explained as poс╣гaka, nourisher

+Jamison Brereton

Drive yon, bounteous one, and drive hither. Brother Indra, in both places there is a goal for you,
where there is a resting place for your lofty chariot and unhitching for your prizewinning donkey.

+Griffith

Depart, O Maghavan;again come hither: both there and here thy goat is Indra, Brother,
Where thy tall chariot hath a place to rest in, and where thqu loosest thy loud-neighing Courser.

+Geldner

Geh fort, du Gabenreicher, und komm wieder, Bruder Indra; an beiden Orten hast du ein Ziel, wo man den hohen Wagen einstellt und den siegreichen Esel ausspannt.

+Grassmann

Geh dorthin, starker, und auch hierher komme, o Indra, Bruder, hier und dort ist Heil dir; Dort wo dir ist des grossen Wagens Schauer und deines schnellen Eselhengstes Einkehr.

+Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWhen you have drunk the Soma, then, Indra, go home; an auspicious life (abides) plural asantly in your dwelling; in either (case) there is the standing in your car or liberating the steeds for provender.тАЭ

accompanied by (priestly) gifts for your prizewinner.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThese (sacrificers) are the Bhojas, of whom the diversified Aс╣Еgirasas (are the priests); and the heroic sons of the expeller (of the foes of the gods) from heaven, bestowing riches upon Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra at the sacrifice of a thousand (victims), prolong (his) life.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

These sacrificers are the Bhojas: ime bhoj─Б aс╣Еgiraso vir┼лp─Б: bhoj─Б = kс╣гatriya descendants of Sud─Бs, sud─Бsaс╕е kс╣гatriya, y─Бgam kurv─Бс╣Зaс╕е, instrumental tuting the sacrifice at which the latter, Medh─Бtithi, and the rest of the race of aс╣Еgiras were their y─Бjakas, or officiating priests; the expeller: rudra, his sons are the maruts; sacrifice of a thousand victims: sahasrasave = the a┼Ыvamedha

+Jamison Brereton

giving bounties to Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra at the Pressing of a Thousand, lengthen their own lifetime.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMaghavan becomes repeatedly (manifest) in various forms, practising delusions with respect to his own peculiar person n; and invoked by his appropriate prayers, he comes in a moment from heaven to the three (daily rites), and, although observant of seasons, is the drinker (of the Soma) irrespective of season.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Form after form the bounteous one assumes, wrapping his own body in tricks,
when three times a day he has come here from heaven in an instant,
drinking out of turn by (the power of) his own (magic) spells, (though) he possesses the truth.

+Griffith

Maghavan weareth every shape at pleasure, effecting magic changes in his body,
Holy One, drinker out of season, coming thrice, in a moment, through fit prayers, from heaven.

+Geldner

In jegliche Gestalt ver├дndert sich der Gabenreiche, am eignen Leib Verwandlungen annehmend, wann er dreimal des Tages auf einen Augenblick gekommen ist oder nach eigenem Ratschlu├Я au├Яer den Zeiten trinkt, der die rechte Ordnung einh├дlt.

+Grassmann

Andre und andre Gestalt nimmt der M├дchtige [Indra] an, Zauberbilder schaffend um seinen Leib, wenn dreimal des Tages er herbeikommt in einem Augenblick, nach eignem Ermessen ausser der Zeit trinkend, der heilige.

+Elizarenkova

The genitive rator of the gods: devaj─Бс╕е = the genitive rator of radiances or energies, tejas─Бm janayit─Б; arrested the watery stream: astabhn─Бt sindhum arс╣Зavam: he is said to have stoped the current of the confluence of the vip─Бs/─Б and ┼Ыutudri rivers; indra with the ku┼Ыikas was plural ased: apriyayata ku┼Ыikebhir Indra = ku┼Ыikagotrotpannair с╣Ыс╣гibhiс╕е saha, with the с╣Ыс╣гis of the ku┼Ыika lineage, or it might be rendered, plural ased by the Ku┼Ыikas

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSages and saints overlookers of the leaders (of sacred rites), Ku┼Ыikas, when the Soma is expresssed with stones at the sacrifice, then exhilarating (the gods) with praises, sing the holy strain (aloud) like (screaming) swans, and, together with the gods, drink the sweet juice of the Soma.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Like geese, you make a signaling call with the pressing stones,
becoming exhilarated on hymns at the ceremony when (the soma) is pressed. You inspired seers who have the sight of men, along with the gods
drink the somian honey, you Ku┼Ыikas.

+Griffith

Like swans, prepare a song of praise with pressing-stones, glad in your hymns with juice poured forth in sacrifice.
Ye singers, with the Gods, sages who look on men, ye Kutikas drink up the Soma’s savoury meath.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

Wie G├дnse macht ihr L├дrm mit den Somasteinen mit Liedern sprudelnd an dem Opferfeste bei dem Saft; mit den G├╢ttern, o begeisterte M├дnner, leitende S├дnger, trinkt ihr, o Ku├зiker, den s├╝ssen Soma.

English translation:

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Made Indra glorified: indram atuс╣гс╣нavam– the verb is the third preterite of the casual, I have caused to be praised; it may mean: I praise Indra, abiding between heaven and earth, i.e. in the firmament

I who have praised both these two world-halves here and IndraтАФ Vi┼Ыv─БmitraтАЩs sacred formulation here guards the Bharata people.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhat do the cattle for you among the K─лkaс╣нas; they yield no milk to mix with the Soma, they need not the vessel (for the libation); bring them to us; (bring also) the wealth of the son of the usurer, and give us Maghavan, (the possessions) of the low branches (of the community).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The K─лkaс╣нas: (Nirukta 6.32) are people who do not perform worship, who are infidels, n─Бstikas; in countrie sinhabited by an─Бryas (k─лkaс╣н─Б n─Бma de┼Ыon─Бryaniv─Бsaс╕е); na tapanti gharm─Бс╣Зi: harmyam = a house;

Gharm─Бс╣Зi = a vessel termed mah─Бv─лra used at the rite called pragс╣Ыhya: pragс╣Ыh y─Бkhy─Б karmopa yuktam mah─Бv─лrap─Бtram, which the cattle do not warm by yielding their milk to it;

Usurer: ─Б bhara pramagandasya vedas: maganda = kusidin, or usurer, one who says to himself, the money that goes from me will come back doubled, and pra = a patronymic; low branches of the community: naic─Б┼Ы─Бkham, that which belongs to a low (n─лca) branch, or class (┼Ы─Бkha); the posterity born of ┼Ъ┼лdras and the like

+Jamison Brereton

What do the cows do for you among the K─лkaс╣нas? They do not milk out the milk mixture; they do not heat the gharma[=hot]-drink.
Bring here to us the possessions of Pramaganda. Make the descendant of N─лc─Б┼Ы─Бkha subject to us, bounteous one.

+Griffith

Among the Kikatas what do thy cattle? They pour no milky draught, they heat no caldron.
Bring thou to us the wealth of Pramaganda;give up to us, O Maghavan, the low-born.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay she, gliding everywhere, quickly bring us food (suited) to the five races of men; may she, the daughter of the sun whom the grey-haired jamadagnis gave to me, (be) the bestower of new life.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Five races of men: pa├▒cajany─Бsu kс╣Ыс╣гс╣нiс╣гu: five distinctions are restricted to human beings; hence, the reference may be to four castes and barbarians; daughter of the sun: pakс╣гy─Б, the daughter of Pakс╣гa: pakс╣гa nirv─Бhakasya, the distributor of the parts (of the year?), i.e. s┼лryasya, of the sun; bestower of new life: navyam ─Бyur dadh─Бna, having new life or food: mama kurvaс╣З─Б bhavatu

+Jamison Brereton

The squirming, sappy (cow called) Sasarpar─л swiftly brought fame to them among the communities of the five peoples,
having taken on new life (like Dawn, though) in her winglessness, she whom the Palastis and Jamadagnis gave me.

+Griffith

Sasarpari brought glory speedily to these, over the generations of the Fivefold Race;
Daughter of Paksa, she bestows new vital power, she whom the ancient Jamadagnis gave to me.

+Geldner

Die Sasarpari brachte diesen gar bald Ruhm ├╝ber die St├дmme der f├╝nf V├╢lker, die auf meiner Seite stehend mir neues Leben verlieh, die mir die Palasti┬┤s und Jamadagni┬┤s gegeben haben.

+Grassmann

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the horse be steady, the axle be strong, the pole be not defective, the yoke not be rotten; may Indra preserve the two yoke-pins from decay; car with uninjured felloes, be ready for us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The horses: g─Бvau gaccheta iti g─Бvau a┼Ыvau: g─Бv─Б implies those who go, or, in this plural ce, horses; car be ready for us: Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra being about to depart from the sacrifice of Sud─Бs, invokes good fortune for his conveyance

+Jamison Brereton

Let the two oxen be steadfast, the axle firm; let the chariot-pole not be torn off, nor the yoke be broken off.
Let Indra keep the two p─Бtalyas [=pieces of chariot?] from breaking. You with indestructible wheel-rims, escort us.

+Griffith

Strong be the pair of oxen, firm the axles, let not the pole slip nor the yoke be broken.
May Indra, keep the yoke-pins from decaying: attend us, thou whose fellies are uninjured.

+Geldner

Die beiden Rinder sollen ausdauernd sein und fest die Achse. Nicht soll die Deichsel abrei├Яen, nicht das Joch zerbrechen. Indra soll die beiden Wagenst├╝tzen vor Bruch bewahren. Du, dessen Radfelge nicht Schaden nimmt, steh uns zur Seite!

+Grassmann

Stark seien die Riemen, fest die Wagenachse; nicht zersplittere die Deichsel, nicht zerbreche das Joch; Indra bewahre die beiden Radb├╝chsen vor Zertr├╝mmerung, du, dessen Radkr├дnze unversehrt sind, sei uns huldreich.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬGive strength, Indra, to our bodies; give strength to our vehicles; (give) strength to our sons and grandsons; that they may live (long); for you are giver of strength.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Put power in our bodies, power in our draft-oxen, IndraтАФ
power for our kith and kin to live, for you are the giver of power.

+Griffith

O Indra, give our bodies strength, strength to the bulls who draw the wains,
Strength to our seed and progeny that they may live, for thou art he who giveth strength.

+Geldner

St├дrke verleih unseren Leibern, St├дrke unseren Zugstieren, Indra, St├дrke dem leiblichen Samen zum Leben, denn du bist der St├дrkeverleiher!

+Grassmann

Gib, Indra, unsern Leibern Kraft, Kraft unsern Wagenstieren, Kraft zum Leben unsern Kindern und Enkeln, denn du bist es, welcher Kraft gibt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFix firmly the substance of the khayar (axle), give solidity to the ┼Ыi┼Ыu (floor) of the car; strong axle, strongly fixed by us, be strong; cast us not from out of our conveyance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Khayar and ┼Ыi┼Ыu: khadirasya s─Бram is the text;

Khadira = mimosa catechu of which the bolt of the axle is made; while the ┼Ыiс╣Г┼Ыapa, dalbergia sisu furnishes wood for the floor; these are still timber-trees in common use

+Jamison Brereton

Engird yourself in the hardwood of the acacia tree; place strength in the ┼Ыiс╣Г┼Ыap─Б(-wood) in its recoil.
O Axle, you who are firm and were made firm, stay firm. DonтАЩt make us leave off from this journey.

+Griffith

Enclose thee in the heart of Khayar timber, in the car wrought of Sinsapa put firmness.
Show thyself strong, O Axle, fixed and strengthened: throw us not from the car whereon we travel.

+Geldner

Umg├╝rte dich mit der H├дrte Khadiraholzes, leih dem Spandanaholze und dem Simsapaholze Kraft! Fest, festgemacht, bleibe fest, du Achse! Setz uns nicht auf der Fahrt ab!

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay this lord of the forest never desert us nor do us harm; may we travel prosperously home until the stopping (of the car), until the unharnessing (of the steeds).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This lord of the forest: vanaspati, i.e. the timber of which the car is made

+Jamison Brereton

Let this Lord of the Forest [=tree] here not leave us behind and not cause us harm.
(Let there be) well-being all the way to the houses, to the unharnessing, to the unhitching.

+Griffith

Let not this sovran of the wood leave us forlorn or injure us.
Safe may we be until we reach our homes and rest us and unyoke.

+Geldner

Dieser Baum soll uns nicht zur├╝cklassen, noch zu Schaden bringen. Bring uns heil bis nach Hause, bis zum Rastmachen, bis zum Ausspannen!

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, hero,possessor of wealth, protect us this day against our foes with many and excellent defences; may the vile wretch who hates us fall (before us); may the breath of life depart from him whom we hate.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Indra, with your manifold means of help, which are the best possible ones, quicken us today, bounteous champion.
Whoever hates us, let him fall low. Whomever we hate, let breath
leave him.

+Griffith

With various aids this day come to us, Indra, with best aids speed us, Maghavan, thou Hero.
Let him who hatcth us fall headlong downward: him whom we hate let vital breath abandon.

+Geldner

Mit den zahlreichen bestm├╢glichen Hilfen mach uns heute regsam, du gabenreicher Held Indra! Wer uns Feind ist, der soll unterliegen. Wem wir Feind sind, dem soll der Odem ausgehen!

+Grassmann

Erfreu uns heute, o Indra, mit vielen allerbesten H├╝lfen, o m├дchtige Held; wer uns hasst, der falle in die Tiefe, und wen wir hassen, dem gehe aus der Odem.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAs (the tree) suffers pain from the axe, as the ┼Ыimbal flower is (easily) cut off, as the injured cauldron leaking scatters foam, so may mine enemy perish.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The ellipse: as the tree is cut down by the axe, so may the enemy be cut down; as one cuts off without difficulty the flower of the ┼Ыimbal, so may he be destroyed; as the ukh─Б (cauldron) when struck (prahata), and thence leaking (yeс╣гant─л, sravant─л), scatters foam or breath from its mouth, so (dveс╣гс╣нa mad─лya, mantra s─Бmarthyena prahataс╕е san, phenam mukh─Бd udgirtu), may that hater, struck by the power of my prayer vomit foam fromhis mouth

+Jamison Brereton

(Though) he heats his axe all the way through, itтАЩs just a ┼Ыimbala flower he hacks off.
The ukh─Б-pot, (though) boiling, boiling over, just throws off foam,
o Indra.

+Griffith

He heats his very axe, and then cuts a mere Semal blossom off.
O Indra, like a caldron cracked and seething, so he pours out foam.

+Geldner

Er macht ihn hei├Я wie man eine Axt erhitzt, er zerhackt ihn wie den Simbalabaum. Wie ein siedender Topf, der ├╝berkocht, wirft er Schaum aus, o Indra.

+Grassmann

Ein jedes Blatt [pal─Б├з├бm vermuthe ich statt para├з├║m] brennt er hinweg, und jede Bl├╝te bricht ab; jeder Topf, o Indra, wenn er kocht und ├╝bersiedet, wirft er Schaum.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMen, (the might) of the destroyer is not known toyou; regarding him as a mere animal, they lead him away desirous (silently to complete his devotions); the wise condescend not to turn the foolish into ridicule, they do not lead the ass before the horse.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra was seized and bound by the followers of Vasiс╣гс╣нha, when observing a vow of silence. These were the reflections of the sage on the occasion: disparaging the rivalry of Vasiс╣гс╣нha with himself, as if between an ass and a horse: s─Бyakasya = of an arrow;here explained, to destroy, avas─Бnak─Бriс╣Зaс╕е; lodham nayanti = they lead the sage;

Lodha = from lubdham, desirous that his penance might not be frustrated, tapasaс╕е kс╣гayo m─Б bh┼лd iti, lobhena tuс╣гс╣З─лm sthitam с╣Ыс╣гim pa┼Ыum manyam─Бna, thinking the с╣Ыс╣гi silent through his desire, to be an animal, i.e., stupid; another interpretation in Nirukta:lubdham с╣Ыс╣гim nayanti pa┼Ыum manyam─Бnaс╕е, they take away the desiring с╣Ыс╣гi, thinking him an animal; na av─Бjinam v─Бjin─Б h─Бsayanti: v─Бjina = from vac, speed, with ina affix; interpreted as srvaj├▒a, all knowing; the contrary avajina = m┼лrkha, a fool

+Jamison Brereton

There is no notice taken of his missile, you people. They lead a lump, thinking it a beast.
(But) they are not making a non-prizewinner race with a prizewinner, nor leading a donkey before the horses.

+Griffith

Men notice not the arrow, O ye people; they bring the red beast deeming it a bullock.
A sluggish steed men run not with the courser, nor ever lead an ass before a charger.

+Geldner

Nicht versteht er sich auf das Wurfgescho├Я, ihr Leute. Sie lenken ein Lodharo├Я, indem sie es f├╝r ein Opfertier halten. Nicht l├д├Яt man einen Klepper mit dem Rennpferd wettlaufen, nicht f├╝hrt man einen Esel als Vorspann vor das Pferd.

+Grassmann

Nicht nimmt man wahr des fliegenden Geschosses, o Leute, nicht reiset man [n├б yanti statt nayanti] einen Fuchs (?) f├╝r ein Zugvieh haltend, nicht l├дsst man ein tr├дges Ross mit einem raschen wettrennen, nicht f├╝hrt man den Esel vor den Rossen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThese sons of Bharata, Indra, understand severance (from the Vasiс╣гс╣нhas), not association (with them); they urge their steeds (against them) as against a constant foe; they bear a stout bow (for their destruction) in battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sons of Bharata: descendants of Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra whose enmity to the lineage of Vasiс╣гс╣нha is here expressed; the enmity reportedly occurred on account of Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra’s disciple the R─Бj─Б sud─Бs; Anukramaс╣Зik─Б states that Vasiс╣гс╣нhas hear not the inimical imprecations: antya abhi┼Ыaparthas ta vasiс╣гс╣нadevaс╣гiс╣Зyaс╕е na vasiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зvanti;

Niruktam: sa vasiс╣гс╣нhadveс╣г─л с╣Ыk-aham ca kapiс╣гс╣нhalo vasi.с╣гhaс╕е atas tana nirbrav─лmi, this and the previous verse are inimical to the Vasiс╣гс╣нhas and he is of the race of Vasiс╣гс╣нha, of the Kapiс╣гс╣нhala branch

+Jamison Brereton

Are these the sons of Bharata, Indra? They take note of the non-meal, not the meal.
They spur the alien horse, not their own. At the contest they lead
around the one whose prize is (just) a bowstring.

+Griffith

These men, the sons of Bharata, O Indra, regard not severance or close connexion.
They urge their own steed as it were another’s, and take him, swift as the bow’s string, to battle.

+Geldner

Indra! Diese S├╢hne des Bharata verstehen sich nur auf das Abfallen, nicht auf den Endlauf. Sie spornen das eigene Ro├Я an, als w├дre es ein fremdes; sie f├╝hren den Renner, der die Schnellkraft einer Bogensehne hat, beim Wettlauf im Kreise herum.

+Grassmann

O Indra, diese S├╢hne des Bharata haben das Ferne im Auge, nicht das Nahe, sie entsenden [beim Wettrennen] das eigne Ross gleichwie ein fremdes; das sehnenstarke f├╝hren sie zum Wettlauf.

+Elizarenkova
